TITLE: Load and Use createDeployment
DESCRIPTION: Loads the `createDeployment` function from the @vercel/client package and demonstrates its usage within an async function. It iterates over deployment events to capture the 'ready' event and retrieve the deployment payload.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/client/README.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
const { createDeployment } = require('@vercel/client');

async function deploy() {
  let deployment;

  for await (const event of createDeployment({
    token: process.env.TOKEN,
    path: '/Users/me/Code/myproject',
  })) {
    if (event.type === 'ready') {
      deployment = event.payload;
      break;
    }
  }

  return deployment;
}
```

TITLE: Using Environment Variables in Vercel
DESCRIPTION: This snippet illustrates how to access environment variables within a Vercel deployment, commonly used for API keys or configuration settings.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/zola-v0/themes/feather/content/my-first-post.md#_snippet_44

LANGUAGE: TypeScript
CODE:
```
export async function GET(request: Request) {
  const apiKey = process.env.API_KEY;
  return new Response(JSON.stringify({ apiKey }), {
    headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
  });
}
```

TITLE: Vercel Project Configuration (vercel.json)
DESCRIPTION: This example shows a basic vercel.json configuration file, which allows customization of build settings, redirects, and headers for Vercel deployments.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/zola-v0/themes/feather/content/my-first-post.md#_snippet_8

LANGUAGE: json
CODE:
```
{
  "version": 2,
  "builds": [
    {
      "src": "package.json",
      "use": "@vercel/static-build",
      "config": {"includeFiles": "public/**"}
    }
  ],
  "routes": [
    {
      "src": "/(.*)",
      "dest": "/$1"
    }
  ]
}

```

TITLE: Handling API Routes in Next.js on Vercel
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to create API routes within a Next.js application deployed on Vercel. API routes allow you to build backend functionalities.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/zola-v0/themes/feather/content/my-first-post.md#_snippet_70

LANGUAGE: TypeScript
CODE:
```
import type { NextApiRequest, NextApiResponse } from 'next'

type Data = {
  name: string
}

export default function handler(
  req: NextApiRequest,
  res: NextApiResponse<Data>
) {
  res.status(200).json({ name: 'John Doe' })
}
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Handling API Routes in Next.js on Vercel
DESCRIPTION: A basic example of an API route in a Next.js application deployed on Vercel. This route handles GET requests and returns a JSON response. It's a common pattern for building backends.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/zola-v0/themes/feather/content/my-first-post.md#_snippet_61

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
export default function handler(req, res) {
  if (req.method === 'GET') {
    res.status(200).json({ name: 'John Doe' });
  } else {
    res.setHeader('Allow', ['GET']);
    res.status(405).end(`Method ${req.method} Not Allowed`);
  }
}
```

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/functions/docs/modules/index.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: typescript

TITLE: Bash Script for Replacing Bootstrap Process with Wrapper
DESCRIPTION: This bash script shows how to replace the current bootstrap process with the Lambda runtime wrapper. It checks if AWS_LAMBDA_EXEC_WRAPPER is set, unsets it for the wrapper execution, and then executes the wrapper with the original script's arguments.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/DEVELOPING_A_RUNTIME.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
#!/bin/bash

if [[ -n $AWS_LAMBDA_EXEC_WRAPPER ]]
  __WRAPPER=$AWS_LAMBDA_EXEC_WRAPPER
  AWS_LAMBDA_EXEC_WRAPPER=""
  exec $__WRAPPER "$0" "${@}"
fi

# start the actual runtime functionality
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Implement Build Function
DESCRIPTION: The required `build` function creates a Serverless Function. It takes build options and returns the output and any necessary routes.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/DEVELOPING_A_RUNTIME.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { BuildOptions, createLambda } from '@vercel/build-utils';

export async function build(options: BuildOptions) {
  // Build the code here…

  const lambda = createLambda(/* … */);
  return {
    output: lambda,
    routes: [
      // If your Runtime needs to define additional routing, define it here…
    ],
  };
}
```

TITLE: Storybook Configuration: Load Assets and Resources
DESCRIPTION: Explains how to load assets and resources in Storybook using the `staticDirs` configuration option. It includes an `Image` component for a visual representation and a link to the relevant documentation.

        width={0}
        height={0}
        style={{ width: '100%', height: 'auto' }} 
        src={Assets} 
        alt="A representation of typography and image assets" 
      />
      <div>
        <h4 className="sb-section-item-heading">Load assets and resources</h4>
        <p className="sb-section-item-paragraph">To link static files (like fonts) to your projects and stories, use the
        `staticDirs` configuration option to specify folders to load when
        starting Storybook.</p>
        <a
          href="https://storybook.js.org/docs/react/configure/images-and-assets"
          target="_blank"
        >Learn more<RightArrow /></a>
      </div>
    </div>
```

TITLE: Nunjucks Include for Post List
DESCRIPTION: This Nunjucks include file (`_includes/postlist.njk`) demonstrates how to create a reusable component to display a list of blog posts.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/eleventy-2/README.md#_snippet_9

LANGUAGE: njk
CODE:
```
{% macro postlist(posts) %}
  <ul class="postlist">
    {% for post in posts %}
      <li class="postlist-item{% if post.url == page.url %} postlist-item-active{% endif %}">
        <a href="{{ post.url }}" class="postlist-link">{{ post.title }}</a>
        <span class="postlist-date">{{ post.date | htmlDateString }}</span>
      </li>
    {% endfor %}
  </ul>
{% endmacro %}
```

TITLE: Rename Files with @vercel/build-utils
DESCRIPTION: The `rename` function from `@vercel/build-utils` is used to modify the paths within a Files object. It accepts the Files object and a mapping function that defines how each path should be transformed. This is useful for tasks like removing file extensions.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/DEVELOPING_A_RUNTIME.md#_snippet_21

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { rename } from '@vercel/build-utils';
```

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
const rename = require('@vercel/build-utils')
const originalFiles = { 'one.go': fileFsRef1, 'two.go': fileFsRef2 }
const renamedFiles = rename(originalFiles, path => path.replace(/\.go$/, ''))
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Implement PrepareCache Function
DESCRIPTION: An optional function to prepare cached files after a build. It returns an object of `File`s to be pre-populated for future builds, speeding up dependency installation.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/DEVELOPING_A_RUNTIME.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { relative } from 'path';
import { glob, PrepareCache } from '@vercel/build-utils';

export const prepareCache: PrepareCache = async ({ 
  workPath,
  repoRootPath,
}) => {
  // Create a mapping of file names and `File` object instances to cache here…
  const rootDirectory = relative(repoRootPath, workPath);
  const cache = await glob(`${rootDirectory}/some/dir/**`, repoRootPath);
  return cache;
};
```

TITLE: Rust VST Plugin Implementation
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates the implementation of a VST plugin in Rust, including macro usage and the `Plugin` trait. This snippet is useful for audio plugin development.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/zola-v0/themes/feather/content/my-first-post.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: rust
CODE:
```
#[macro_use]
extern crate vst;

// We're implementing a trait `Plugin` that does all the VST-y stuff for us.
impl Plugin for Whisper {
    fn get_info(&self) -> Info {
        Info {
            name: "Whisper".to_string()
        }
    }
}
```

TITLE: Bash Script for Runtime Wrapper Execution
DESCRIPTION: This bash script demonstrates how to execute a Lambda runtime, conditionally using a wrapper if the AWS_LAMBDA_EXEC_WRAPPER environment variable is set. It passes the runtime path and parameters to the wrapper.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/DEVELOPING_A_RUNTIME.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
#!/bin/bash

exec $AWS_LAMBDA_EXEC_WRAPPER path/to/runtime param1 param2
```

TITLE: Execute Command with Counter
DESCRIPTION: This JavaScript function demonstrates a simple counter increment operation. It initializes a counter, increments it, and logs a test message to the console. This snippet is useful for basic scripting and testing.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/eleventy-2/posts/thirdpost.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
function myCommand() {
  let counter = 0;

  counter++;
}

// Test with a line break above this line.
console.log('Test');
```

TITLE: Handle Featured Image in Vercel Project
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to handle featured images in a Vercel project using Hugo templating. It trims leading slashes from the image path and generates an absolute URL to ensure the image displays correctly regardless of the site's location. The code also includes logic to display the image as a link to the post if a featured image is present.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/hugo-v0/themes/ananke/layouts/partials/summary-with-image.html#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: go
CODE:
```
{{ $featured_image := .Params.featured_image }}

{{ if .Params.featured_image }} {{/* Trimming the slash and adding absURL make sure the image works no matter where our site lives */}} {{ $featured_image := (trim $featured_image "/") | absURL }}

[![image from {{ .Title }}]({{ $featured_image }})]({{.URL}})

{{ end }}

[{{ .Title }}]({{.URL}})

{{ .Summary }}

[{{ $.Param "read_more_copy" | default (i18n "readMore") }}]({{.URL}}) {{/* TODO: add author

By {{ .Author }}

*/}}

TITLE: Handle Featured Image in Vercel Project
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to handle featured images in a Vercel project using Hugo templating. It trims leading slashes from the image path and generates an absolute URL to ensure the image displays correctly regardless of the site's location. The code also includes logic to display the image as a link to the post if a featured image is present.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/cli/test/dev/fixtures/08-hugo/themes/ananke/layouts/partials/summary-with-image.html#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: go
CODE:
```
{{ $featured_image := .Params.featured_image }}

{{ if .Params.featured_image }} {{/* Trimming the slash and adding absURL make sure the image works no matter where our site lives */}} {{ $featured_image := (trim $featured_image "/") | absURL }}

[![image from {{ .Title }}]({{ $featured_image }})]({{.URL}})

{{ end }}

[{{ .Title }}]({{.URL}})

{{ .Summary }}

[{{ $.Param "read_more_copy" | default (i18n "readMore") }}]({{.URL}}) {{/* TODO: add author

By {{ .Author }}

*/}}
```

TITLE: Attach Database Pool (TypeScript)

CODE:

const pgPool = new Pool({
  connectionString: process.env.DATABASE_URL,
});
attachDatabasePool(pgPool);
```

TITLE: Implement startDevServer for Vercel CLI
DESCRIPTION: This function is an optional export used by `vercel dev` to provide an optimized development experience. It spawns a child process that creates an HTTP server and returns the listening port and the child process's PID. The child process communicates the port via file descriptor 3.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/DEVELOPING_A_RUNTIME.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { spawn } from 'child_process';
import { StartDevServerOptions } from '@vercel/build-utils';

export async function startDevServer(options: StartDevServerOptions) {
  // Create a child process which will create an HTTP server.
  //
  // Note: `my-runtime-dev-server` is an example dev server program name.
  // Your implementation will spawn a different program specific to your runtime.
  const child = spawn('my-runtime-dev-server', [options.entrypoint], {
    stdio: ['ignore', 'inherit', 'inherit', 'pipe'],
  });

  // In this example, the child process will write the port number to FD 3…
  const portPipe = child.stdio[3];
  const childPort = await new Promise(resolve => {
    portPipe.setEncoding('utf8');
    portPipe.once('data', data => {
      resolve(Number(data));
    });
  });

  return { pid: child.pid, port: childPort };
}
```

TITLE: TypeScript Serverless Function for Vercel
DESCRIPTION: An example of a serverless function written in TypeScript for Vercel. This function demonstrates type safety and returns a greeting. It requires TypeScript to be configured in the project.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/zola-v0/themes/feather/content/my-first-post.md#_snippet_64

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { VercelRequest, VercelResponse } from '@vercel/node';

export default (request: VercelRequest, response: VercelResponse) => {
  const { name = 'World' } = request.query;
  response.status(200).send(`Hello ${name}!`);
};
```

TITLE: Handle Featured Image in Vercel Project
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to handle featured images in a Vercel project using Hugo templating. It trims leading slashes from the image path and generates an absolute URL to ensure the image displays correctly regardless of the site's location. The code also includes logic to display the image as a link to the post if a featured image is present.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/examples/hugo/themes/ananke/layouts/partials/summary-with-image.html#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: go
CODE:
```
{{ $featured_image := .Params.featured_image }}

{{ if .Params.featured_image }} {{/* Trimming the slash and adding absURL make sure the image works no matter where our site lives */}} {{ $featured_image := (trim $featured_image "/") | absURL }}

[![image from {{ .Title }}]({{ $featured_image }})]({{.URL}})

{{ end }}

[{{ .Title }}]({{.URL}})

{{ .Summary }}

[{{ $.Param "read_more_copy" | default (i18n "readMore") }}]({{.URL}}) {{/* TODO: add author

By {{ .Author }}

*/}}
```

LANGUAGE: JavaScript
CODE:
```
export default function handler(req, res) {
  res.status(200).send('Hello from Vercel Serverless Function!');
}
```

TITLE: Eleventy Configuration Example
DESCRIPTION: This snippet shows a typical Eleventy configuration file, `.eleventy.js`, where you can customize site settings, template formats, and more.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/eleventy-2/README.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
// Example content of .eleventy.js
module.exports = function(eleventyConfig) {
  // Add custom collections, filters, shortcodes, etc.
  // Configure template formats
  eleventyConfig.setTemplateFormats(['njk', 'md', 'html', 'liquid', 'css', 'png']);

  // Copy static assets
  eleventyConfig.addPassthroughCopy('images');

  return {
    dir: {
      input: '.',
      output: '_site'
    }
  };
};
```

TITLE: Eleventy Configuration Example
DESCRIPTION: This snippet shows a typical Eleventy configuration file, `.eleventy.js`, where you can customize site settings, template formats, and more.

  // Add custom collections, filters, shortcodes, etc.
  // Configure template formats

  // Copy static assets
  eleventyConfig.addPassthroughCopy('images');

  return {
    dir: {
      input: '.',
      output: '_site'
    }
  };
};
```

TITLE: Creating a Vercel Project Configuration
DESCRIPTION: This snippet shows how to create a `vercel.json` file to configure project settings, including redirects and headers.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/zola-v0/themes/feather/content/my-first-post.md#_snippet_42

LANGUAGE: JSON
CODE:
```
{
  "redirects": [
    {
      "source": "/old-page",
      "destination": "/new-page"
    }
  ],
  "headers": [
    {
      "source": "/_next/static/(.*)",
      "headers": [
        {
          "key": "Cache-Control",
          "value": "public, max-age=31536000, immutable"
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
}
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Configure Polymer Root Path
DESCRIPTION: Sets the root path for the Polymer application. This is crucial for correctly serving the app from either the root directory or a sub-directory. It defines a global variable `MyAppGlobals` to store this path.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/polymer-v3/index.html#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
/**
 * [polymer-root-path]
 *
 * Leave this line unchanged if you intend to serve your app from the root
 * path (e.g., with URLs like `my.domain/` and `my.domain/view1`).
 *
 * If you intend to serve your app from a non-root path (e.g., with URLs
 * like `my.domain/my-app/` and `my.domain/my-app/view1`), edit this line
 * to indicate the path from which you'll be serving, including leading
 * and trailing slashes (e.g., `/my-app/`).
 */
window.MyAppGlobals = { rootPath: '/' };
```

TITLE: Render Social Media Links with Icons (Hugo)
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to conditionally render social media links with corresponding SVG icons. It uses Hugo's `with` and `partial` functions to check for parameters and include SVG partials. The `icon_size` variable is set to '32px' for consistent icon sizing. Each link includes an SVG icon, a new window icon, and the platform's URL, along with descriptive alt text.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/hugo-v0/themes/ananke/layouts/partials/social-follow.html#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: html
CODE:
```

TITLE: Continue Request Processing with Next()
DESCRIPTION: Returns a Response that allows the system to continue processing the request. This is useful in middleware for passing control to the next handler. It can optionally accept initialization options for the response.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/functions/docs/modules/index.md#_snippet_25

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { next } from '@vercel/edge';

export default function middleware(_req: Request) {
  return next();
}
```

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { next } from '@vercel/edge';

export default function middleware(_req: Request) {
  return next({
    headers: { 'x-from-middleware': 'true' },
  });
}
```

TITLE: Implement ShouldServe Function
DESCRIPTION: An optional function used by `vercel dev` to determine if a Runtime should handle a specific request path. It returns a boolean indicating responsibility.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/DEVELOPING_A_RUNTIME.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { ShouldServeOptions } from '@vercel/build-utils';

export async function shouldServe(options: ShouldServeOptions) {
  // Determine whether or not the Runtime should respond to the request path here…

  return options.requestPath === options.entrypoint;
}
```

TITLE: Configure Polymer Root Path
DESCRIPTION: Sets the root path for the Polymer application. This is crucial for correctly serving the app from either the root directory or a sub-directory. It defines a global variable `MyAppGlobals` to store this path.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/examples/polymer/index.html#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
/**
 * [polymer-root-path]
 *
 * Leave this line unchanged if you intend to serve your app from the root
 * path (e.g., with URLs like `my.domain/` and `my.domain/view1`).
 *
 * If you intend to serve your app from a non-root path (e.g., with URLs
 * like `my.domain/my-app/` and `my.domain/my-app/view1`), edit this line
 * to indicate the path from which you'll be serving, including leading
 * and trailing slashes (e.g., `/my-app/`).
 */
window.MyAppGlobals = { rootPath: '/' };
```

TITLE: Fetch Date from Node.js API (JavaScript)

}

--------------------------------

TITLE: Define and Implement a Tool in TypeScript
DESCRIPTION: Example of defining a tool named 'add' using Zod for schema validation and TypeScript for implementation. It includes schema definition, metadata, and the tool's logic to add two numbers.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/examples/xmcp/README.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import {
  z
} from "zod";
import {
  type InferSchema
} from "xmcp";

// Define the schema for tool parameters
export const schema = {
  a: z.number().describe("First number to add"),
  b: z.number().describe("Second number to add"),
};

// Define tool metadata
export const metadata = {
  name: "add",
  description: "Add two numbers together",
  annotations: {
    title: "Add Two Numbers",
    readOnlyHint: true,
    destructiveHint: false,
    idempotentHint: true,
  },
};

// Tool implementation
export default async function add({ a, b }: InferSchema<typeof schema>) {
  return {
    content: [{
      type: "text",
      text: String(a + b)
    }],
  };
}
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: glob and download Example - JavaScript
DESCRIPTION: An example demonstrating the combined use of download and glob. It first downloads all files and then uses glob to return a Files representation of the entire directory.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/DEVELOPING_A_RUNTIME.md#_snippet_19

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
const { glob, download } = require('@vercel/build-utils');

exports.build = ({ files, workPath }) => {
  await download(files, workPath);
  return glob('**', workPath);
};
```

{{ .Content }}

{{/* Define a section to pull recent posts from. For Hugo 0.20 this will default to the section with the most number of pages. */}} {{ $mainSections := .Site.Params.mainSections | default (slice "post") }} {{/* Create a variable with that section to use in multiple places. */}} {{ $section := where .Site.RegularPages "Section" "in" $mainSections }} {{/* Check to see if the section is defined for ranging through it */}} {{ $section_count := len $section }} {{ if ge $section_count 1 }} {{/* Derive the section name */}} {{ $section_name := index (.Site.Params.mainSections) 0 }}

{{/* Use $section_name to get the section title. Use "with" to only show it if it exists */}} {{ with .Site.GetPage "section" $section_name }}

{{ $.Param "recent_copy" | default (i18n "recentTitle" .) }}
=============================================================

{{ end }} {{ $n_posts := $.Param "recent_posts_number" | default 3 }}

{{/* Range through the first $n_posts items of the section */}} {{ range (first $n_posts $section) }}

{{ partial "summary-with-image.html" . }}

{{ end }}

{{ if ge $section_count (add $n_posts 1) }}

{{ i18n "more" }}
=================

{{/* Now, range through the next four after the initial $n_posts items. Nest the requirements, "after" then "first" on the outside */}} {{ range (first 4 (after $n_posts $section)) }}

[{{ .Title }}({{ .URL }})]
--------------------------

{{ end }} {{/* As above, Use $section_name to get the section title, and URL. Use "with" to only show it if it exists */}} {{ with .Site.GetPage "section" $section_name }} [{{ i18n "allTitle" . }}({{ .URL }})]({{ .URL }}) {{ end }}

{{ end }}

{{ end }}

{{ end }}
```

{{/* Use $section_name to get the section title. Use "with" to only show it if it exists */}} {{ with .Site.GetPage "section" $section_name }}

{{ $.Param "recent_copy" | default (i18n "recentTitle" .) }}
=============================================================

{{ end }} {{ $n_posts := $.Param "recent_posts_number" | default 3 }}

{{/* Range through the first $n_posts items of the section */}} {{ range (first $n_posts $section) }}

{{ partial "summary-with-image.html" . }}

{{ end }}

{{ if ge $section_count (add $n_posts 1) }}

{{ i18n "more" }}
=================

{{/* Now, range through the next four after the initial $n_posts items. Nest the requirements, "after" then "first" on the outside */}} {{ range (first 4 (after $n_posts $section)) }}

[{{ .Title }}({{ .URL }})]
--------------------------

{{ end }} {{/* As above, Use $section_name to get the section title, and URL. Use "with" to only show it if it exists */}} {{ with .Site.GetPage "section" $section_name }} [{{ i18n "allTitle" . }}({{ .URL }})]({{ .URL }}) {{ end }}

TITLE: Create Blog Post Markdown

TITLE: Test Vercel Joke List Command with Telemetry
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to write a unit test for the 'vercel joke list' command using Vitest. It shows how to simulate command-line arguments, invoke the command, and assert the expected telemetry events are tracked using a mocked client and the `toHaveTelemetryEvents` helper.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/cli/src/util/telemetry/README.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import joke from '../../../../src/commands/joke';

it('tracks humor level', async () => {
  client.setArgv('joke', 'list', '10'); // build up the simulated command line segments
  const exitCode = await joke(client); // call the command function
  expect(exitCode, 'exit code for "joke"').toEqual(0); // ensure the command reaches completion with success

  // ensure the store has the items you expect
  expect(client.telemetryEventStore).toHaveTelemetryEvents([
    {
      key: `subcommand:list`,
      value: 'ls',
    },
    {
      key: `argument:joke-level`,
      value: '10',
    },
  ]);
});
```

TITLE: Next: Continue Request Processing
DESCRIPTION: The 'next' function returns a Response that allows the system to continue processing the request. It can optionally accept an 'init' object to add headers to the response.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/edge/docs/README.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { next } from '@vercel/edge';

export default function middleware(_req: Request) {
  return next();
}
```

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { next } from '@vercel/edge';

export default function middleware(_req: Request) {
  return next({
    headers: { 'x-from-middleware': 'true' },
  });
}
```

CODE:
```
import { normalizeRoutes } from '@vercel/routing-utils';

const { routes, error } = normalizeRoutes(inputRoutes);

  console.log(error.code, error.message);
}
```

TITLE: JavaScript: Creating a Reusable Component
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates the creation of a simple, reusable component using JavaScript. This promotes modularity and code reuse in larger projects.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/zola-v0/themes/feather/content/my-first-post.md#_snippet_57

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
function createButton(text, onClick) {
  const button = document.createElement('button');
  button.textContent = text;
  button.addEventListener('click', onClick);
  return button;
}

const myButton = createButton('Click Me', () => {
  alert('Button clicked!');
});
document.body.appendChild(myButton);
```

TITLE: JavaScript: Fetching Data from an API
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to fetch data from a remote API using the `fetch` function in JavaScript. This is a common pattern for retrieving data in web applications.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/zola-v0/themes/feather/content/my-first-post.md#_snippet_55

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
async function fetchData(url) {
  try {
    const response = await fetch(url);
    if (!response.ok) {
      throw new Error(`HTTP error! status: ${response.status}`);
    }
    const data = await response.json();
    console.log(data);
    return data;
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error fetching data:', error);
  }
}
```

TITLE: Hugo Site Title Configuration
DESCRIPTION: Configures the site's title and page title using Hugo's templating system. It includes logic to append the page's specific title if available and incorporates the Hugo generator tag.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/hugo-v0/themes/ananke/layouts/_default/baseof.html#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: Go

TITLE: Display Recent Posts in Hugo
DESCRIPTION: This Go HTML template snippet defines a section to display recent posts. It defaults to the 'post' section and allows configuration of the number of posts to show. It also includes logic to display a 'more' link and additional posts.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/examples/hugo/themes/ananke/layouts/index.html#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: go-html-template
CODE:
```
{{ define "main" }}

{{ .Content }}

{{/* Define a section to pull recent posts from. For Hugo 0.20 this will default to the section with the most number of pages. */}} {{ $mainSections := .Site.Params.mainSections | default (slice "post") }} {{/* Create a variable with that section to use in multiple places. */}} {{ $section := where .Site.RegularPages "Section" "in" $mainSections }} {{/* Check to see if the section is defined for ranging through it */}} {{ $section_count := len $section }} {{ if ge $section_count 1 }} {{/* Derive the section name */}} {{ $section_name := index (.Site.Params.mainSections) 0 }}

{{/* Use $section_name to get the section title. Use "with" to only show it if it exists */}} {{ with .Site.GetPage "section" $section_name }}

{{ $.Param "recent_copy" | default (i18n "recentTitle" .) }}
=============================================================

{{ end }} {{ $n_posts := $.Param "recent_posts_number" | default 3 }}

{{/* Range through the first $n_posts items of the section */}} {{ range (first $n_posts $section) }}

{{ partial "summary-with-image.html" . }}

{{ end }}

{{ if ge $section_count (add $n_posts 1) }}

{{ i18n "more" }}
=================

{{/* Now, range through the next four after the initial $n_posts items. Nest the requirements, "after" then "first" on the outside */}} {{ range (first 4 (after $n_posts $section)) }}

[{{ .Title }}({{ .URL }})]
--------------------------

{{ end }} {{/* As above, Use $section_name to get the section title, and URL. Use "with" to only show it if it exists */}} {{ with .Site.GetPage "section" $section_name }} [{{ i18n "allTitle" . }}({{ .URL }})]({{ .URL }}) {{ end }}

{{ end }}

{{ end }}

{{ end }}
```

TITLE: createLambda Example - JavaScript
DESCRIPTION: An example demonstrating the creation of a Lambda instance using createLambda and FileBlob, specifying the runtime, handler, and file content.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/DEVELOPING_A_RUNTIME.md#_snippet_15

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
const { createLambda, FileBlob } = require('@vercel/build-utils');
await createLambda({
  runtime: 'nodejs8.10',
  handler: 'index.main',
  files: {
    'index.js': new FileBlob({ data: 'exports.main = () => {}' }),
  },
});
```

TITLE: Hugo Template Configuration
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates Hugo template configurations for setting the site title, page title, and generator. It also includes conditional logic for production environments and the inclusion of custom CSS stylesheets.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/cli/test/dev/fixtures/08-hugo/themes/ananke/layouts/_default/baseof.html#_snippet_0

CODE:

{{ .Hugo.Generator }}
{{/* NOTE: For Production make sure you add `HUGO_ENV="production"` before your build command */}}
{{ if eq (getenv "HUGO_ENV") "production" | or (eq .Site.Params.env "production") }}  {{ else }}  {{ end }}
{{ $stylesheet := .Site.Data.webpack_assets.app }}
{{ with $stylesheet.css }}  {{ end }}
{{ range .Site.Params.custom_css }}  {{ end }}
```

TITLE: Debug @vercel/nft Tree-Shaking
DESCRIPTION: This JavaScript code snippet uses the @vercel/nft library to trace dependencies of an entry point file. It helps identify missing files during the tree-shaking process, indicating potential issues within the @vercel/nft library itself.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/README.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
const { nodeFileTrace } = require('@vercel/nft');
nodeFileTrace(['path/to/entrypoint.js'], {
  ts: true,
  mixedModules: true,
})
  .then(o => console.log(o.fileList))
  .then(e => console.error(e));
```

TITLE: Register Service Worker
DESCRIPTION: Registers a Service Worker for pre-caching assets. This code checks for Service Worker support in the browser and, if available, registers the 'service-worker.js' file with the scope defined by `MyAppGlobals.rootPath`.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/polymer-v3/index.html#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
// Load and register pre-caching Service Worker
if ('serviceWorker' in navigator) {
  window.addEventListener('load', function() {
    navigator.serviceWorker.register('service-worker.js', { scope: MyAppGlobals.rootPath });
  });
}
```

{% endfor %}

TITLE: Rewrite Request Destination
DESCRIPTION: Returns a response that rewrites the current request to a different URL. This function is used to internally redirect the request to another path without changing the URL in the browser. It can be used with optional initialization parameters.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/functions/docs/modules/index.md#_snippet_26

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { rewrite, next } from '@vercel/edge';

export default async function middleware(req: Request) {
  const flagged = await getFlag(req, 'isExperimental');
  if (flagged) {
    const url = new URL(req.url);
    url.pathname = `/experimental{url.pathname}`;
    return rewrite(url);
  }

  return next();
}
```

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { rewrite, next } from '@vercel/edge';

export default function middleware(req: Request) {
  const auth = checkJwt(req.headers.get('Authorization'));
  if (!checkJwt) {
    return rewrite(new URL('/api/error-unauthorized', req.url));
  }
  const url = new URL(req.url);
  url.searchParams.set('_userId', auth.userId);
  return rewrite(url);
}

export const config = { matcher: '/api/users/:path*' };
```

TITLE: CSS Styling for Storybook Components
DESCRIPTION: Defines CSS styles for various Storybook components, including headings, link lists, link items, and tips, to ensure a consistent and visually appealing presentation.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/cli/test/fixtures/unit/commands/build/storybook-with-middleware/stories/Introduction.mdx#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: css
CODE:
```
.subheading {
  --mediumdark: '#999999';
  font-weight: 700;
  font-size: 13px;
  color: #999;
  letter-spacing: 6px;
  line-height: 24px;
  text-transform: uppercase;
  margin-bottom: 12px;
  margin-top: 40px;
}

.link-list {
  display: grid;
  grid-template-columns: 1fr;
  grid-template-rows: 1fr 1fr;
  row-gap: 10px;
}

@media (min-width: 620px) {
  .link-list {
    row-gap: 20px;
    column-gap: 20px;
    grid-template-columns: 1fr 1fr;
  }
}

@media all and (-ms-high-contrast:none) {
  .link-list {
    display: -ms-grid;
    -ms-grid-columns: 1fr 1fr;
    -ms-grid-rows: 1fr 1fr;
  }
}

.link-item {
  display: block;
  padding: 20px;
  border: 1px solid #00000010;
  border-radius: 5px;
  transition: background 150ms ease-out, border 150ms ease-out, transform 150ms ease-out;
  color: #333333;
  display: flex;
  align-items: flex-start;
}

.link-item:hover {
  border-color: #1EA7FD50;
  transform: translate3d(0, -3px, 0);
  box-shadow: rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.08) 0 3px 10px 0;
}

.link-item:active {
  border-color: #1EA7FD;
  transform: translate3d(0, 0, 0);
}

.link-item strong {
  font-weight: 700;
  display: block;
  margin-bottom: 2px;
}

.link-item-img-wrapper {
  height: 40px;
  width: 40px;
  margin-right: 15px;
  flex: none;
}

.link-item span,
.link-item p {
  margin: 0;
  font-size: 14px;
  line-height: 20px;
}

.tip {
  display: inline-block;
  border-radius: 1em;
  font-size: 11px;
  line-height: 12px;
  font-weight: 700;
  background: #E7FDD8;
  color: #66BF3C;
  padding: 4px 12px;
  margin-right: 10px;
  vertical-align: top;
}

.tip-wrapper {
  font-size: 13px;
  line-height: 20px;
  margin-top: 40px;
  margin-bottom: 40px;
}

.tip-wrapper code {
  font-size: 12px;
  display: inline-block;
}
```

TITLE: Register Service Worker
DESCRIPTION: Registers a Service Worker for pre-caching assets. This code checks for Service Worker support in the browser and, if available, registers the 'service-worker.js' file with the scope defined by `MyAppGlobals.rootPath`.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/examples/polymer/index.html#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
// Load and register pre-caching Service Worker
if ('serviceWorker' in navigator) {
  window.addEventListener('load', function() {
    navigator.serviceWorker.register('service-worker.js', { scope: MyAppGlobals.rootPath });
  });
}
```

{{ .Hugo.Generator }}
{{/* NOTE: For Production make sure you add `HUGO_ENV="production"` before your build command */}}
{{ if eq (getenv "HUGO_ENV") "production" | or (eq .Site.Params.env "production") }}  {{ else }}  {{ end }}
{{ $stylesheet := .Site.Data.webpack_assets.app }}
{{ with $stylesheet.css }}  {{ end }}
{{ range .Site.Params.custom_css }}  {{ end }}
```

TITLE: Rewrite: Redirect Request to New URL
DESCRIPTION: The 'rewrite' function returns a Response that rewrites the current request to a specified destination URL. This is useful for feature flagging or conditional routing. It can take a URL string or a URL object as the destination.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/edge/docs/README.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { rewrite, next } from '@vercel/edge';

export default async function middleware(req: Request) {
  const flagged = await getFlag(req, 'isExperimental');
  if (flagged) {
    const url = new URL(req.url);
    url.pathname = `/experimental{url.pathname}`;
    return rewrite(url);
  }

  return next();
}
```

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { rewrite, next } from '@vercel/edge';

export default function middleware(req: Request) {
  const auth = checkJwt(req.headers.get('Authorization'));
  if (!checkJwt) {
    return rewrite(new URL('/api/error-unauthorized', req.url));
  }
  const url = new URL(req.url);
  url.searchParams.set('_userId', auth.userId);
  return rewrite(url);
}

export const config = { matcher: '/api/users/:path*' };
```

TITLE: Vercel Edge Function waitUntil for Error Reporting
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates using the waitUntil method of the RequestContext to send error details to an external tracking service. This ensures that error reporting occurs even if the main response is sent with an error status.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/edge/docs/interfaces/RequestContext.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import type { RequestContext } from '@vercel/edge';

export async function handleRequest(
  request: Request,
  ctx: RequestContext
): Promise<Response> {
  try {
    return await myFunctionThatReturnsResponse();
  } catch (e) {
    ctx.waitUntil(
      (async () => {
        // report this error to your error tracking service
        await fetch('https://my-error-tracking-service.com', {
          method: 'POST',
          body: JSON.stringify({
            stack: e.stack,
            message: e.message,
            name: e.name,
            url: request.url,
          }),
        });
      })()
    );
    return new Response('Internal Server Error', { status: 500 });
  }
}
```

TITLE: Hugo Configuration for Comments

TITLE: Reference Hosts of Related Projects with TypeScript
DESCRIPTION: Reference the hosts of related Vercel projects using the `withRelatedProject` function. This utility allows specifying a project name and a fallback default host, useful for dynamic API endpoint resolution.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/related-projects/README.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { withRelatedProject } from '@vercel/related-projects';

const apiHost = withRelatedProject({
  projectName: 'my-api-project',
  // used as a fallback
  defaultHost: process.env.API_HOST,
});

// This can replace all usages of:
// const apiHost = process.env.API_HOST;
```

TITLE: Query TXT Records with nslookup

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/errors/cant-solve-challenge.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: bash
CODE:
```
nslookup -q=TXT _acme-challenge.domain.com
```

TITLE: Hugo Main Content Template
DESCRIPTION: Defines the main content block, displaying the current section title, page title, formatted date, reading time, word count, and content. It also includes partials for tags and comments.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/static-build/test/fixtures/hugo-v0/themes/ananke/layouts/_default/single.html#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: Go
CODE:
```
{{ define "main" }} {{ $section := .Site.GetPage "section" .Section }} {{/* CurrentSection allows us to use the section title instead of inferring from the folder. https://gohugo.io/variables/page/#section-variables-and-methods */}} {{with .CurrentSection.Title }}{{. | upper }}{{end}}

{{- .Title -}}
==============

{{/* Hugo uses Go's date formatting is set by example. Here are two formats */}} {{- .Date.Format "January 2, 2006" -}} {{/* Show "reading time" and "word count" but only if one of the following are true: 1) A global config `params` value is set `show_reading_time = true` 2) A section front matter value is set `show_reading_time = true` 3) A page front matter value is set `show_reading_time = true` */}} {{ if (or (eq (.Param "show_reading_time") true) (eq $section.Params.show_reading_time true) )}} - {{ .ReadingTime}} minutes read - {{ .WordCount}} words {{ end }}

{{- .Content -}} {{- partial "tags.html" . -}}

{{ if .Site.DisqusShortname }} {{ template "_internal/disqus.html" . }} {{ end }} {{ if .Site.Params.commentoEnable }} {{- partial "commento.html" . -}} {{ end }}

{{- partial "menu-contextual.html" . -}}

{{ end }}
```

TITLE: Validate Routes using routesSchema with Ajv
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to validate a routing configuration against the `routesSchema` provided by `@vercel/routing-utils` using the Ajv library. It compiles the schema and checks the validity of a sample route array.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/routing-utils/README.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: ts
CODE:
```
import { routesSchema } from '@vercel/routing-utils';

const ajv = new Ajv();
const validate = ajv.compile(routesSchema);
const valid = validate([{ src: '/about', dest: '/about.html' }]);

if (!valid) console.log(validate.errors);
```

TITLE: Check Rate Limit with @vercel/firewall
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to use the `checkRateLimit` function from the `@vercel/firewall` package to enforce rate limits on API routes. It checks a specific rate limit identifier and returns a 429 Too Many Requests response if the limit is reached.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/firewall/README.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: ts
CODE:
```
import { checkRateLimit } from '@vercel/firewall';

export async function POST() {
  const { rateLimited } = await checkRateLimit('my-rate-limit-id');
  if (rateLimited) {
    return new Response('', {
      status: 429,
    });
  }
  // Implement logic guarded by rate limit
}
```

TITLE: Hugo Related Content
DESCRIPTION: This snippet shows how to implement Hugo's related content feature. It fetches up to 15 related pages based on parameters like tags and displays them as a list with links to their respective pages. This feature helps in content discovery.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/examples/hugo/themes/ananke/layouts/partials/menu-contextual.html#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: go
CODE:
```
{{/* Use Hugo's native related content feature to pull in content that may have similar parameters, like tags. etc. https://gohugo.io/content-management/related/ */}}
{{ $related := .Site.RegularPages.Related . | first 15 }}
{{ with $related }}

{{ i18n "related" }}

{{ range . }}
*   [{{- .Title -}}]({{ .RelPermalink }})
{{ end }}

{{ end }}
```

  --mediumdark: '#999999';

  text-transform: uppercase;
  margin-bottom: 12px;
  margin-top: 40px;
}

.link-list {
  display: grid;
  grid-template-columns: 1fr;
  grid-template-rows: 1fr 1fr;
  row-gap: 10px;
}

@media (min-width: 620px) {
  .link-list {
    row-gap: 20px;
    column-gap: 20px;

  }

    -ms-grid-rows: 1fr 1fr;
  }

  display: block;
  padding: 20px;
  border: 1px solid #00000010;
  border-radius: 5px;

  font-weight: 700;

  margin-bottom: 2px;

  height: 40px;
  width: 40px;
  margin-right: 15px;
  flex: none;
}

.link-item p {
  margin: 0;
  font-size: 14px;
  line-height: 20px;
}

.tip {

TITLE: Get Vercel OIDC Token (Async)
DESCRIPTION: Retrieves the current OIDC token asynchronously from the request context or environment variable. This function should not cache the token as it can change. It handles token expiration by refreshing it in development environments.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/functions/docs/modules/oidc.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
getVercelOidcToken()
  .then(token => {
    console.log('OIDC Token:', token);
  })
  .catch(error => {
    console.error('Error:', error.message);
  });
```

TITLE: Get Vercel OIDC Token (Sync)
DESCRIPTION: Retrieves the current OIDC token synchronously from the request context or environment variable. This function does not refresh expired tokens. It's crucial not to cache the returned token due to potential changes.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/functions/docs/modules/oidc.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
const token = getVercelOidcTokenSync();
console.log('OIDC Token:', token);
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Get Vercel OIDC Token (Sync)
DESCRIPTION: Retrieves the OIDC token synchronously from the request context or environment variable. This function does not refresh expired tokens and should not be cached. It throws an error if the token is unavailable.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/oidc/docs/README.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
import { getVercelOidcTokenSync } from '@vercel/oidc';

function getTokenSync() {
  try {
    const token = getVercelOidcTokenSync();
    console.log('OIDC Token:', token);
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error:', error.message);
  }
}
```

TITLE: Fix RegExp Syntax in Vercel Custom Route Source
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to fix an invalid custom route `source` in Vercel by correctly wrapping RegExp syntax, like negative lookaheads, as an un-named parameter using `path-to-regexp`'s conventions. This ensures proper parsing of routes with complex matching requirements.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/errors/invalid-route-source.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
{
  source: '/feedback/(?!general)',
  destination: '/api/feedback/general'
}
```

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
{
  source: '/feedback/((?!general).*)',
  destination: '/api/feedback/general'
}
```

TITLE: AwsCredentialsProviderInit Properties
DESCRIPTION: Defines the properties for initializing the awsCredentialsProvider, including optional and required fields for AWS STS client configuration, duration, logging, and role assumption parameters.

interface AwsCredentialsProviderInit {
  clientConfig?: any;
  clientPlugins?: Pluggable<any, any>[];
  durationSeconds?: undefined | number;
  logger?: Logger;
  parentClientConfig?: {
    region?: string | Provider<string>;
  };
  policy?: undefined | string;
  policyArns?: undefined | { arn?: string }[];
  providerId?: undefined | string;
  roleArn: string;

}

TITLE: Hugo Main Content Template
DESCRIPTION: Defines the main content block, displaying the current section title, page title, formatted date, reading time, word count, and content. It also includes partials for tags and comments.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/examples/hugo/themes/ananke/layouts/_default/single.html#_snippet_1

CODE:
```
{{ define "main" }} {{ $section := .Site.GetPage "section" .Section }} {{/* CurrentSection allows us to use the section title instead of inferring from the folder. https://gohugo.io/variables/page/#section-variables-and-methods */}} {{with .CurrentSection.Title }}{{. | upper }}{{end}}

{{- .Title -}}
==============

{{/* Hugo uses Go's date formatting is set by example. Here are two formats */}} {{- .Date.Format "January 2, 2006" -}} {{/* Show "reading time" and "word count" but only if one of the following are true: 1) A global config `params` value is set `show_reading_time = true` 2) A section front matter value is set `show_reading_time = true` 3) A page front matter value is set `show_reading_time = true` */}} {{ if (or (eq (.Param "show_reading_time") true) (eq $section.Params.show_reading_time true) )}} - {{ .ReadingTime}} minutes read - {{ .WordCount}} words {{ end }}

{{- .Content -}} {{- partial "tags.html" . -}}

{{ if .Site.DisqusShortname }} {{ template "_internal/disqus.html" . }} {{ end }} {{ if .Site.Params.commentoEnable }} {{- partial "commento.html" . -}} {{ end }}

{{- partial "menu-contextual.html" . -}}

{{ end }}
```

TITLE: AwsCredentialsProviderInit Interface
DESCRIPTION: Defines the structure for initializing the AWS credentials provider, allowing customization of STS client configurations, role assumption parameters, and session details.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/functions/docs/interfaces/oidc.AwsCredentialsProviderInit.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
interface AwsCredentialsProviderInit extends Omit<FromWebTokenInit, "webIdentityToken"> {
  clientConfig?: any;
  clientPlugins?: Pluggable<any, any>[];
  durationSeconds?: undefined | number;
  logger?: Logger;
  parentClientConfig?: Object & {
    region?: string | Provider<string>;
  };
  policy?: undefined | string;
  policyArns?: undefined | { arn?: string }[];
  providerId?: undefined | string;
  roleArn: string;
  roleAssumerWithWebIdentity?: (params: AssumeRoleWithWebIdentityParams) => Promise<AwsCredentialIdentity>;
}
```

TITLE: Modify Headers with Vercel Edge Middleware
DESCRIPTION: This example demonstrates how to add a custom header ('x-user-id') and remove an existing header ('authorization') from an incoming request using Vercel's Edge middleware. It utilizes the `rewrite` function and manipulates the `Headers` object.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/edge/docs/interfaces/ModifiedRequest.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { rewrite } from '@vercel/edge';

export default async function middleware(request: Request): Promise<Response> {
  const newHeaders = new Headers(request.headers);
  newHeaders.set('x-user-id', 'user_123');
  newHeaders.delete('authorization');
  return rewrite(request.url, {
    request: { headers: newHeaders },
  });
}
```

TITLE: Get Vercel OIDC Token (Async)
DESCRIPTION: Retrieves the OIDC token asynchronously from the request context or environment variable. This function can refresh expired tokens in development environments. It's recommended not to cache the token as it may change.

TITLE: Get Vercel Runtime Cache (TypeScript)
DESCRIPTION: Retrieves an instance of the Vercel Runtime Cache. The cache can be configured with options like custom key hashing functions or namespaces for organizing cache entries. It ensures data consistency and efficient retrieval.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/functions/docs/modules/index.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import { getCache } from '@vercel/functions';

const cache = getCache({
  namespace: 'my-app',
  keyHashFunction: (key) => `custom-hash-${key}`
});
```

TITLE: Check Rate Limit with @vercel/firewall
DESCRIPTION: This function allows you to check if a request is rate-limited according to rules defined in the Vercel Firewall. It takes a `rateLimitId` and optional configuration, returning a promise that resolves with rate limiting status. It's useful for implementing custom rate-limiting logic in your Vercel Functions.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/firewall/docs/README.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
import { unstable_checkRateLimit as checkRateLimit } from '@vercel/firewall';

export async function POST() {
  const { rateLimited } = await checkRateLimit('my-rate-limit-id');
  if (rateLimited) {
    return new Response('', {
      status: 429,
    });
  }
  // Implement logic guarded by rate limit
}
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Runtime API Interface
DESCRIPTION: Defines the structure of a Vercel Runtime, including required and optional methods for building and serving applications.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/DEVELOPING_A_RUNTIME.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
interface Runtime {
  version: number;
  build: (options: BuildOptions) => Promise<BuildResult>;
  prepareCache?: (options: PrepareCacheOptions) => Promise<CacheOutputs>;
  shouldServe?: (options: ShouldServeOptions) => Promise<boolean>;
  startDevServer?: (
    options: StartDevServerOptions
  ) => Promise<StartDevServerResult>;
}
```

TITLE: Get Geolocation Information (JavaScript)
DESCRIPTION: Retrieves location details for an incoming request. The function returns an object containing city, country, region, latitude, and longitude. It's useful for geo-targeting or location-based features.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/functions/docs/modules/index.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
import { geolocation } from '@vercel/functions';

export function GET(request) {
  const details = geolocation(request);
  return Response.json(details);
}
```

TITLE: AWS Credentials Provider
DESCRIPTION: Provides an AWS credential identity provider. This function takes an initialization object containing details for fetching AWS credentials.

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
awsCredentialsProvider(init: AwsCredentialsProviderInit): AwsCredentialIdentityProvider;
```

TITLE: Create AWS Credentials Provider with Vercel OIDC
DESCRIPTION: This example demonstrates how to use the `awsCredentialsProvider` function to create an AWS credential provider. It configures an S3 client with credentials obtained via Vercel's OIDC, specifying various options like `roleArn`, `clientConfig`, and custom `roleAssumerWithWebIdentity`.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/oidc-aws-credentials-provider/docs/README.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: js
CODE:
```
import * as s3 from '@aws-sdk/client-s3';
import { awsCredentialsProvider } from '@vercel/functions/oidc';

const s3Client = new s3.S3Client({
  credentials: awsCredentialsProvider({
    roleArn: 'arn:aws:iam::1234567890:role/RoleA',
    clientConfig: { region: 'us-west-2' },
    clientPlugins: [addFooHeadersPlugin],
    roleAssumerWithWebIdentity: customRoleAssumer,
    roleSessionName: 'session_123',
    providerId: 'graph.facebook.com',
    policyArns: [{ arn: 'arn:aws:iam::1234567890:policy/SomePolicy' }],
    policy:
      '{"Statement": [{"Effect": "Allow", "Action": "s3:ListBucket", "Resource": "*"}]}',
    durationSeconds: 7200,
  }),
});

```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Vercel Edge Function RequestContext Example
DESCRIPTION: An example demonstrating how to use the RequestContext in a Vercel Edge Function. It shows the basic structure of an Edge Function handler that receives both the Request and RequestContext objects.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/edge/docs/interfaces/RequestContext.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: typescript
CODE:
```
import type { RequestContext } from '@vercel/edge';

export default async function handler(
  request: Request,
  ctx: RequestContext
): Promise<Response> {
  // ctx is the RequestContext
}
```

TITLE: Ensure Parameter Consistency in Vercel Custom Routes
DESCRIPTION: This snippet illustrates how to fix an 'Invalid Custom Route `source`' error in Vercel by ensuring that all segments used in the `destination` property are also present in the `source` property. This is crucial for Vercel's routing mechanism to correctly map requests to destinations.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/errors/invalid-route-source.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
{
  source: '/feedback/:type',
  destination: '/api/feedback/:id'
}
```

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
{
  source: '/feedback/:id',
  destination: '/api/feedback/:id'
}
```

TITLE: Hugo Header Template
DESCRIPTION: Defines the header block in a Hugo template, allowing for overrides and inclusion of partials like 'page-header.html'.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/examples/hugo/themes/ananke/layouts/_default/single.html#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: Go
CODE:
```
{{ define "header" }} {{/* We can override any block in the baseof file be defining it in the template */}} {{ partial "page-header.html" . }} {{ end }}
```

TITLE: Get Request IP Address
DESCRIPTION: Retrieves the IP address of an incoming request from the headers. It accepts either a Request object or Headers object as input. The function returns the IP address as a string or undefined if it cannot be determined.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/functions/docs/modules/index.md#_snippet_24

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
import { ipAddress } from '@vercel/functions';

export function GET(request) {
  const ip = ipAddress(request);
  return new Response(`Your IP is ${ip}`);
}
```

TITLE: Get IP Address - JavaScript
DESCRIPTION: Retrieves the IP address of the incoming request from the headers using the 'ipAddress' function from the @vercel/functions package. It can accept either a Request object or a Headers object as input.

SOURCE: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/packages/edge/docs/README.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
import { ipAddress } from '@vercel/functions';

export function GET(request) {
  const ip = ipAddress(request);
  return new Response(`Your IP is ${ip}`);
}
```
